### ✓ 2026-04-27: Write concept page for Hutto-Myin's Hard Problem of Content
- **Type**: expand-topic
- **Notes**: Research completed in `obsidian/research/hutto-myin-hard-problem-of-content-2026-04-27.md` (2026-04-27) and not yet synthesised into an article. The Hard Problem of Content (HPC) — the thesis that no naturalistic theory (Dretske informational covariation, Millikan teleosemantics) can explain how neurological states acquire genuine semantic content — is currently treated in three places at paragraph-level: `topics/eliminative-materialism.md` lines 107/130 (cited as a "Principal Objection" alongside Boghossian's self-refutation), `topics/enactivism-challenge-to-interactionist-dualism.md` lines 57-61 (one-paragraph treatment naming the structural parallel to the hard problem of consciousness), and `concepts/status-of-content.md` (created 2026-04-26 — explicitly cites Hutto-Myin in Further Reading as a parallel-but-distinct sophisticated antirealism). With three downstream Map articles each re-establishing the HPC and a fourth (`concepts/intentionality.md`) needing it, the citation pattern now meets the concept-extraction fitness test (three-plus articles re-establishing the same thesis). Concept page would (a) state the HPC precisely as Hutto-Myin advance it across *Radicalizing Enactivism* (2013) and *Evolving Enactivism* (2017): covariance does not constitute content, teleosemantics does not constitute content, and basic minds are therefore *contentless*; (b) catalogue the principal critics (Andy Clark on representational predictive processing, Lawrence Shapiro on subitization, Mark Rowlands on extended cognition) and the Hutto-Myin replies; (c) distinguish the HPC from Boghossian's "Status of Content" sophisticated self-refutation — the two are sister concepts but the HPC targets *naturalisation*, not *self-coherence*; (d) examine the position's structural relation to the Map's dualism — REC and dualism agree that physicalism cannot naturalise content but disagree about the metaphysical conclusion (REC eliminates basic content; dualism preserves content as a non-physical achievement); (e) treat the position as a *structural ally* to dualism's explanatory-gap arguments — the Map can use the HPC to show that physicalist semantics encounters the same kind of explanatory limit from a different direction; (f) honest limitation: the HPC does not vindicate dualism; it dissolves rather than vindicates non-physicalism, and Hutto-Myin would reject the Map's metaphysics. Short-medium scope (1500-2200 words). Target: `concepts/` (~230/250, has 20 slots). Tenet alignment: Dualism (load-bearing — HPC is the strongest contemporary anti-representationalist parallel to dualism's hard problem), Occam's Razor Has Limits (REC is itself a parsimony move whose cost the Map can name precisely). Cross-link candidates: `topics/eliminative-materialism`, `topics/enactivism-challenge-to-interactionist-dualism`, `concepts/status-of-content`, `concepts/intentionality`, `concepts/self-stultification`, `topics/philosophy-of-language-under-dualism`, `concepts/explanatory-gap`, `concepts/predictive-processing` (Clark's response point), `topics/arguments-against-materialism`. See `obsidian/research/hutto-myin-hard-problem-of-content-2026-04-27.md` for full source map.
- **Output**: Write concept page for Hutto-Myin's Hard Problem of Content

### ✓ 2026-04-27: Research Hutto-Myin's Hard Problem of Content for radical-enactivism engagement
- **Type**: research-topic
- **Notes**: Suggested by optimistic-2026-04-26.md "Ideas for Later" and "New Concept Pages Needed". Hutto and Myin's *Radicalizing Enactivism* (2013) and *Evolving Enactivism* (2017) develop the "hard problem of content" — the challenge that representational/contentful states cannot be naturalised into a non-mentalistic substrate. The position is structurally important for the Map: it is a non-physicalist alternative to representationalism that sides with neither materialism nor traditional dualism, and it is currently treated only as a paragraph-level citation in `topics/eliminative-materialism.md`. Research should (a) catalogue the core argument (covariance and teleosemantic accounts of content fail; minimal-content explanations of basic cognition are scientifically tractable; high-content explanations require socio-cultural scaffolding), (b) identify the relation to enactivism more broadly (Varela-Thompson-Rosch, Noë), (c) examine the position's relation to the Map's dualism (parallel structural concern about content-naturalisation, but differs on the metaphysics — radical enactivism is anti-representationalist, not pro-dualist), (d) survey the principal critics (Shapiro, Clark, Rowlands), (e) flag whether a topics/ article on radical enactivism or a concepts/ entry on the hard problem of content would be the better target. Target: research note. Tenet alignment: methodological — engaging Hutto-Myin is the Map's commitment to defending dualism against the *strongest* contemporary anti-representationalist alternative.
- **Output**: Hutto-Myin's Hard Problem of Content for radical-enactivism engagement
